#### (1) Structural Result

This chapter shows that dysfunctional dynamics are rarely sudden. They are prepared where binding demand becomes covert, asymmetry becomes difficult to name, non-events steer, attractors fixate, distance erodes, and temporality hardens what the frame still narrates as local or reversible.

Within that preparation, several drift overlays become readable: pseudo-symmetry, sexed leniency drift, asymmetric self-control burden, humiliation-near overload, outer-form denial, visible-form fixation, boundary-aggression collapse, and the sexual drift triad of asymmetry-switch drift, parity-to-exit, and responsibility-to-authority.

The chapter does not turn these markers into new operators. It uses them as scene-bound drift overlays: ways of seeing when a configuration is becoming less governable, less interruptible, less integrable, or less D-compatible under Θ.

#### (2) Cost Distribution

The costs of destructive dynamics appear through accumulation: **over time**, hidden binding becomes harder to deny; through **repetition**, scripts and categories become easier than alternatives; through **asymmetry**, access, exposure, definition, and responsibility distribute unevenly; through **sex-coded leniency**, relief and blame may stop tracking actual operator load; through **asymmetric self-control burden**, one role-position may carry disproportionate Χ/Ψ demand; through **humiliation-near repetition**, distance and self-binding can become overloaded; through **visible-form fixation**, deeper cost topology may be under-read; through **outer-form denial**, enacted form may be immunized; through **boundary-aggression collapse**, interruption and harm become harder to distinguish; through **publicness**, already active readability may be amplified and sedimentized; and through **irreversibility**, exits become more expensive as paths harden.

#### (3) Structural Viability Corridor

**Viability increases where** asymmetry is nameable, cost topology remains explicit, self-binding does not leak covertly, leniency tracks scene and responsibility rather than sex-coded readability, self-control burdens are paired with dignity recognition, categories remain proportional to the broader sexual field, humiliation-near forms remain bounded and re-readable, boundary-setting remains distinguishable from aggression, visible form is taken seriously without being totalized, internal framing remains accountable to outer form, and asymmetry activation remains marked, bounded, and re-bound into Σ/Ψ.

**Drift begins where** binding enters silently, pseudo-symmetry hides cost, categories replace frame breadth, access simulation replaces concrete correction, body/boundary coding becomes person truth, sexed leniency replaces operator reading, one role-position carries disproportionate self-control without recognition, humiliation-near repetition overloads Χ/Ψ, visible form is either denied or totalized, boundary and aggression collapse into each other, asymmetry activation becomes unmarked, parity becomes exit, or responsibility becomes authority.

#### (4) Entry Guard

* **Χ (Distance):** preserved by making drift markers readable as configuration-language, not as person verdicts, moral leverage, or practical-instruction language. Χ also requires that stopping, re-reading, refusal, boundary-setting, and interruption remain structurally distinguishable from aggression.
* **Reversibility:** preserved by treating every marker as scene-bound and revisable, without claiming that accumulated Θ effects can be erased.
* **D (Dignity-in-Practice):** preserved by naming destructive dynamics without humiliation, diagnosis, sex truth, moral rank, or violence authorization. D fails where asymmetry becomes leverage, parity becomes abandonment, responsibility becomes control, visible form becomes total person judgment, or self-control burden erases dignity recognition.

#### (5) Structural Viability Verdict

Dysfunctional dynamics become destructive where they reduce governability: Χ weakens, Σ cannot integrate, Ψ leaks covertly, Ω becomes unnameable or turns into leverage, Θ breaks the reset fiction, and D can no longer be preserved without denying part of the configuration.

Sexual reciprocity under real asymmetry does not require equal burdens. It requires that unequal burdens not be externalized through unmarked asymmetry activation, parity-to-exit, responsibility-to-authority, sexed leniency drift, asymmetric self-control burden, visible-form fixation, outer-form denial, or boundary-aggression collapse.

#### (6) One-line Marker

Dysfunctional dynamics are rarely sudden: they are prepared when Ψ leaks, Ω steers, Χ erodes, Α fixates, Θ breaks the reset fiction, and reciprocity fails through asymmetry-leverage, parity-exit, responsibility-authority, or collapsed boundary readability.

---

## 19. Functional Conditions and Warning Signals

*(Criteria, not practical instruction; Chapter 19 uses markers operationally and references the dynamics from Chapter 18 rather than repeating them.)*

This chapter analyzes enactments, roles, and scenes. It provides criteria only: no practical instruction, no diagnosis, no person labels, no moral ranking, no sex truth, and no violence authorization. Risk notes remain praxeological markers.

### 19.1 Purpose of the Chapter

This chapter provides a configuration-bound viability lens: minimal conditions under which sexual practice remains functionally viable, plus warning signals indicating drift. The lens does not issue norms or person judgments; it evaluates scenes by cost layout, frame legibility, outer readability, category pressure, publicness awareness, and trajectory realism—without typing persons.

Functional viability is not established by benign internal naming alone. It depends on whether the enacted configuration remains governable under asymmetry, temporality, non-events, distance, and dignity constraints, including where outer form remains more demanding than the scene’s own self-description suggests.

After Chapters 15–18, this chapter also treats category formation, access-threshold pressure, body/boundary coding, humiliation-nearness, visible-form fixation, asymmetric self-control burden, and boundary-aggression collapse as viability-relevant only where they affect scene governability. They are not person descriptions, sex truths, diagnoses, or practical rules.

### 19.2 Minimal Formula

**Δ → ∇ → □ → Λ → Α → Ω → Θ → Φ → Χ → Σ → Ψ**

In this chapter, the arrows that pull most are **Ω → Θ** and the feedback effects of accumulated Θ on Ω layouts, with **Χ** as the stabilizing limiter. **Ψ leak**, **Φ inflation**, **outer-form denial**, **visible-form fixation**, **category monopolization**, **after-scene dignity failure**, **sexed leniency drift**, **asymmetric self-control burden**, **boundary-aggression collapse**, and **publicness confusion** function as early drift multipliers.

This formula follows the default PMS repository dependency path. The chapter does not add a new operator or alter PMS v1.3; it uses the default chain as a viability lens for PMS-SEX.

### 19.3 Functional Minimum Conditions

> **Note:** “functional” means: viable under Ω/Θ/Λ, without systematic dignity violation, without exit fictions, without category monopolization, and without using internal labels to erase enacted form.

#### (1) Explicit Ω recognition

(Ω: contextual meaning = gradients of access, exposure, obligation, and cost-bearing.)

In this configuration:

* cost, risk, access, and exposure gradients are not denied,
* equality rhetoric is not used as a substitute for management,
* uneven exit capacity, repair burden, bodily overhang, or reputational exposure remains nameable,
* asymmetry is treated as a regulable cost topology rather than as a moral accusation.

**Minimal form:** Ω(asymmetry) remains nameable and regulable within the frame.

Naming asymmetry does not rank persons. It preserves the configuration’s readability.

#### (2) Θ awareness

(Θ: contextual meaning = accumulation, irreversibility, and trajectory.)

In this configuration:

* temporality is carried as structure: frequency, repetition, after-effects, repair windows,
* “just this once” narratives do not override visible accumulation,
* recontextualization does not claim rewind,
* exit is treated as trajectory change, not reset,
* after-scene dignity is treated as part of temporal realism rather than as an optional moral add-on.

**Minimal form:** consequences are treated as real: exit realism and after-scene dignity.

#### (3) Stable Χ capacity (stop + meta competence)

(Χ: contextual meaning = stop-capability and meta-position within ongoing praxis.)

In this configuration:

* stop-capability is practically available, not merely asserted,
* distance can be activated before escalation becomes irreversible,
* meta-commentability remains available without punitive framing,
* outer-form awareness is not treated as betrayal, hostility, or moral accusation,
* stopping, refusal, withdrawal, boundary-setting, resistance, and distance creation remain structurally distinguishable from aggressive, punitive, retaliatory, or discharge-driven conduct.

**Minimal form:** Χ(distance) is operative, not ornamental.

#### (4) No Ψ substitution (no covert binding substitute)

(Ψ: contextual meaning = self-binding as identity-relevant attribution over time.)

In this configuration:

* sexual practice does not substitute for integration, self-worth, identity proof, or relationship clarification,
* meaning demands do not cross frame boundaries covertly,
* local scenes are not silently converted into commitment tests,
* non-binding language does not conceal binding effects already active under repetition, exposure, category fixation, or asymmetry.

**Minimal form:** no Ψ leak as the default carrier of stakes.

#### (5) Λ tolerance without escalation

(Λ: contextual meaning = structured absence, delay, or withdrawal under expectation.)

In this configuration:

* non-events—pause, fatigue, unavailability, cancellation, hesitation—are tolerable,
* Λ is not recoded into control, punishment, devaluation, or possession,
* absence remains legible without becoming an interpretive guessing burden,
* non-occurrence does not become the primary steering instrument.

**Minimal form:** Λ(non-event) can exist without becoming steering or coercion.

#### (6) Internal framing remains accountable to outer form

(□ / Φ / Χ: contextual meaning = frame, re-description, and re-reading capacity.)

In this configuration:

* practice labels clarify internal occupation but do not end structural analysis,
* internal meaning is allowed to be real without erasing enacted form,
* outer legibility can be named without becoming person-ranking,
* visible form is taken seriously without being totalized as the whole configuration,
* consent, play, devotion, service, guided dominance, humiliation-nearness, or authenticity language does not block cost-layout analysis.

**Minimal form:** internal framing does not erase outer structural form, and visible form does not exhaust the scene.

#### (7) Publicness is handled as overlay

(□ overlay: contextual meaning = visibility, circulation, documentation, reputation, and sedimentation.)

In this configuration:

* publicity is not treated as the sole origin of consequence,
* publicity is also not ignored where it amplifies, documents, repeats, or sedimentizes consequences,
* publicness remains distinguished from primary scene legibility,
* reputational or documentary effects are tracked as Θ/Ω intensifiers.

**Minimal form:** publicness modifies readability and consequence without being confused with their necessary origin.

#### (8) Category, access, and body/boundary discipline

(Δ / Α / Ω: contextual meaning = difference, category stabilization, and cost topology.)

In this configuration:

* category availability remains proportional to the broader sexual field,
* image-bound or category-bound repetition does not replace frame breadth, distance, or concrete correction,
* access remains threshold-language rather than entitlement,
* access, refusal, exception, and permission-image effects remain distinguishable from consent or encounter,
* body/boundary coding remains scene-bound rather than becoming person truth,
* body-state, exposure, shame, recognition, or boundary-form is not treated as the essence of a role-position.

* self-control burdens are nameable where one role-position carries disproportionate restraint, interruption, de-escalation, or distance,

#### (9) After-scene dignity and burden recognition

(D / Χ / Ψ: contextual meaning = dignity-in-practice, distance, and self-binding under temporal carryover.)

In this configuration:

* humiliation-near, exposure-near, guided-dominance-near, body-marked, or boundary-marked forms remain carryable after the scene,
* after-costs do not require person-shrinking, shame residue, blame reversal, immunity, or self-worth leakage,
* self-control burdens are nameable where one role-position must carry disproportionate restraint, interruption, de-escalation, or distance,
* higher Χ/Ψ burden is paired with higher dignity recognition, not lower recognition,
* leniency tracks scene, cost, capacity, and responsibility rather than sex-coded automatic relief or blame overload.

**Minimal form:** after-scene dignity remains intact, and self-control burdens remain visible as dignity-relevant costs.

### 19.4 Warning Signals

These markers indicate drift potential—toward coercion, harm, or destructive dynamics—without labeling persons. They do not decide concrete cases, authorize response, or provide a legal, tactical, or moral rule. For chaining logic, see Chapter 18.

#### (1) Φ narrative inflation

(Φ: contextual meaning = recontextualization that relocates structure without dissolving costs.)

In this configuration:

* “actually it is…” becomes repeatedly necessary to cover costs or asymmetry,
* re-framing replaces clarification and cost naming,
* later meaning claims are used to erase prior action-form,
* internal description moves while Α/Ω/Θ remain unchanged.

**Structural note:** Φ substitutes for Σ(integration).

#### (2) Narrowing of □ alternatives (mono-frame)

(□: contextual meaning = the scene grammar that defines what counts and what can be named.)

In this configuration:

* only one frame “works,”
* alternatives are devalued or rendered impossible,
* practice labels protect the dominant frame from re-reading,
* the frame becomes readable only through one script.

**Structural note:** Α(attractor) monopolizes □(frame).

#### (3) Ω moralization instead of regulation

(Ω: contextual meaning = cost and access gradients.)

In this configuration:

* asymmetry is not managed but negotiated via moral guilt or entitlement,
* “if you loved me, you would…” becomes the steering device,
* naming asymmetry is treated as accusation,
* outer-form analysis is collapsed into blame.

**Structural note:** Ω is handled ideologically, increasing pseudo-symmetry risk.

#### (4) Persistence despite clear structural undercutting

(Θ: contextual meaning = accumulation and irreversibility.)

In this configuration:

* repetition continues despite visible bodily, reputational, binding-related, or D-violating costs,
* exit is imagined but not executed; exit fiction persists,
* harm is recognized but not structurally interrupted,
* “insight” does not alter the operator chain.

**Structural note:** Α(attractor) + Θ(accumulation) overrun Χ(distance) (dynamic logic: Chapter 18).

#### (5) Externalization of Θ costs

(Θ: contextual meaning = temporal cost and consequence.)

In this configuration:

* consequences are offloaded: bodily, reputational, emotional, social, exposure-related, binding-related,
* the short-term relieved pole stabilizes the configuration at the other’s expense,
* after-costs concentrate in roles less able to refuse or redefine them,
* publicness may sedimentize externalized costs without creating them.

**Structural note:** Θ costs are shifted asymmetrically through Ω(layout).

#### (6) Outer-form denial

(□ / Χ: contextual meaning = frame and meta-reading capacity.)

In this configuration:

* internal naming is used to block structural reading,
* consent-language or practice-labels are treated as sufficient to settle all form,
* outer legibility is treated as merely moralistic, hostile, or public misunderstanding,
* visible action-form remains unread.

**Structural note:** Χ is weakened because the configuration cannot re-read itself.

#### (7) Visible-form fixation

(□ / Λ / Ω / Θ / Χ: contextual meaning = visible action-form within broader configuration.)

In this configuration:

* the most visible action-form is treated as the whole structure,
* frame history, non-event pressure, internal framing, asymmetry distribution, and temporal accumulation are under-read,
* visible outer form is used to settle what only the full configuration can show,
* correction targets only the visible layer while cost topology remains unread.

**Structural note:** visible form matters, but it does not exhaust scene structure.

#### (8) Publicness confusion

(□ overlay / Θ: contextual meaning = frame extension and temporal sedimentation.)

In this configuration:

* publicity is treated as the whole source of harm,
* or publicity is treated as irrelevant despite amplifying exposure and consequence,
* audience reaction replaces scene analysis,
* documentation, circulation, or reputation effects are denied until they harden.

**Structural note:** publicness is misread either as origin or as nothing, rather than as overlay.

#### (9) Category monopolization

(Δ / Α / Θ: contextual meaning = category formation, attractor stabilization, and repetition.)

In this configuration:

* category availability replaces frame breadth,
* what is searchable, repeatable, combinable, or easy to re-enter becomes easier than re-reading,
* category repetition normalizes and then demands new difference,
* alternatives remain possible in theory but lose practical attractiveness.

**Structural note:** category pressure becomes drift where Α monopolizes □.

#### (10) Access entitlement drift

(Ω: contextual meaning = access threshold, refusal, exception, and cost topology.)

In this configuration:

* access language becomes claim language,
* refusal, delay, distance, or non-availability is treated as injury, deprivation, or illegitimate withholding,
* simulated counterdesire or permission-images substitute for concrete correction,
* access thresholds organize the scene while responsibility for their costs is denied.

**Structural note:** access is a structural threshold, not entitlement.

#### (11) Body/boundary person-truth drift

(Δ / Ω / Θ: contextual meaning = body-state, boundary coding, visibility, exposure, and bodily overhang.)

In this configuration:

* body-state, exposure, shame, recognition, or boundary-form is read as the truth of a person,
* a body/boundary category replaces scene-bound reconstruction,
* bodily or reputational overhang is denied while visibility intensifies,
* a role-position is reduced to the category it displays or carries.

**Structural note:** body/boundary coding must remain scene-bound, not person-truth.

#### (12) Sexed leniency drift

(Ω / R / Ψ: contextual meaning = responsibility distribution, role burden, and self-binding load.)

In this configuration:

* leniency or blame tracks sex-coded readability rather than scene, cost, capacity, or responsibility,
* escalation by one role-position is contextualized while another role-position’s boundary, refusal, or distance is over-blamed,
* vulnerability language or danger language replaces operator reading,
* responsibility is displaced through automatic relief or automatic suspicion.

**Structural note:** leniency tracks configuration, not sex-coded expectation.

#### (13) Asymmetric self-control burden

(Χ / Ψ / D: contextual meaning = distance, self-binding, and dignity-in-practice.)

In this configuration:

* one role-position must carry disproportionate restraint, de-escalation, non-reaction, or distance,
* another role-position’s escalation is more easily framed as injury, overwhelm, context, or exception,
* self-control expectation erases the cost of carrying self-control,
* higher Χ/Ψ burden is paired with lower dignity recognition.

**Structural note:** greater self-control burden requires greater dignity recognition, not less.

#### (14) Boundary-aggression collapse

(Χ / Ω / D: contextual meaning = stop-capability, cost topology, and dignity-in-practice.)

In this configuration:

* stopping, refusal, withdrawal, resistance, or distance creation is too quickly read as aggression,
* or aggressive, punitive, retaliatory, discharge-driven, or escalatory conduct is framed as mere boundary-setting,
* the scene can no longer distinguish interruption from attack, or attack from interruption,
* labels settle what only frame, cost topology, temporal accumulation, interruption capacity, and after-scene dignity can reconstruct.

**Structural note:** this marker does not adjudicate concrete cases or authorize response. It marks a failure of scene readability: boundary and aggression can no longer be structurally distinguished.

#### (15) After-scene dignity failure

(D / Θ / Ψ: contextual meaning = dignity-in-practice under temporal carryover.)

In this configuration:

* the scene can only be carried afterward through person-shrinking, blame reversal, degradation, immunity, or self-worth leakage,
* humiliation-nearness or guided dominance is treated as immune because it was internally named as play,
* after-costs are assigned to one role-position without recognition,
* the scene remains locally intelligible only by denying its temporal overhang.

**Structural note:** after-scene dignity is part of Θ realism, not a decorative moral supplement.

### 19.5 Chapter Closure — Viability Criteria and Drift Signals

#### (1) Condensation

This chapter defines functional sexual practice not by normality, but by minimal structural conditions: asymmetry remains nameable, temporality is carried realistically, distance remains operative, binding is not substituted covertly, non-events remain tolerable without becoming steering instruments, internal framing remains accountable to outer form, visible form is taken seriously without being totalized, category pressure stays proportional, access stays non-entitled, body/boundary coding stays scene-bound, after-scene dignity is preserved, and publicness is handled as overlay.

These conditions keep the configuration governable under pressure rather than stabilizing through drift substitutes.

The chapter also clarifies that benign self-description is not enough. A configuration is viable only where its enacted form, category profile, cost distribution, temporal trajectory, boundary readability, and stop-capability remain readable beyond internal labels.

#### (2) Cost Layout

* **Ω layout:** functional configurations render gradients discussable and regulable; drift configurations deny gradients until conflict becomes non-negotiable.
* **Θ layout:** functional configurations treat accumulation and after-scene dignity as real; drift configurations rely on reset narratives until exit collapse or dignity loss becomes likely.
* **Χ layout:** functional configurations preserve stop-capability, meta-position, and boundary readability; drift configurations confuse interruption, withdrawal, refusal, or distance with aggression, or frame aggression as mere boundary-setting.
* **Category layout:** functional configurations keep category availability proportional to the broader sexual field; drift configurations let searchable, repeatable, combinable forms monopolize the frame.
* **Access layout:** functional configurations keep access as threshold-language; drift configurations convert access thresholds into entitlement, deprivation narratives, or simulated counterdesire without concrete correction.
* **Body/boundary layout:** functional configurations keep body-state, exposure, shame, recognition, and boundary-form scene-bound; drift configurations convert them into person truth.
* **□ overlays:** publicity and documentation can amplify downstream costs and reduce reversibility of later re-reads.
* **Outer legibility:** internal naming may fail to settle how the enacted form remains structurally readable.
* **Visible-form guard:** visible form remains readable, but not totalized as the whole configuration.
* **Body remainder:** material consequence capacity can force Θ realism even when frames narrate harmlessness.

#### (3) Structural Reading Corridor

Several readings are structurally warranted as criteria:

* treating Ω as a cost layout rather than a moral contest is rational because it keeps regulation possible,
* treating Θ realism as mandatory is rational because consequences are not resettable by narrative,
* treating Χ as decisive is rational because it is the primary limiter of escalation, fixation, and boundary-aggression collapse,
* treating Ψ leak and Φ inflation as early drift markers is rational because they raise stakes while avoiding explicit frame capacity,
* treating category monopolization as a warning signal is rational because searchable, repeatable, and combinable forms can replace broader frame work,
* treating access as threshold rather than entitlement is rational because people do not owe access,
* treating body/boundary coding as scene-bound is rational because body-state, exposure, shame, or boundary-form does not define person truth,
* treating after-scene dignity as viability-relevant is rational because Θ continues after local enactment,
* treating internal labels as insufficient is rational because practice naming does not settle outer structural form,
* treating visible form as relevant but non-totalizing is rational because outer readability matters without exhausting the configuration,
* treating publicness as overlay is rational because publicity can harden consequence without being its sole origin.

#### (4) Entry Guard

* **Χ (Distance):** maintained by treating stop-capability, meta-reading, boundary readability, and outer-form awareness as continuous functional requirements of viability, not as emergency measures. Loss of practical distance is read as a drift signal, not as lack of commitment. Boundary-setting, stopping, refusal, withdrawal, resistance, and distance creation remain structurally distinguishable from aggressive, punitive, retaliatory, discharge-driven, or escalatory conduct.
* **Reversibility:** maintained by keeping all criteria configuration-bound and revisable, while explicitly acknowledging that accumulated temporal, bodily, exposure-related, reputational, category-bound, and binding costs are not undone by re-interpretation.
* **D (Dignity-in-Practice):** maintained by using viability and warning markers as structural criteria only, without attributing fault, deficit, intent, diagnosis, sex truth, identity rank, or personal worth. D also requires that self-control burdens, humiliation-nearness, body/boundary coding, and after-scene costs be named without turning them into shame, entitlement, immunity, or person judgment.

#### (5) Viability Verdict

Viability increases where Ω is recognized, Θ carried, Χ operative, Ψ not substituted, Λ tolerable, category pressure proportional, access non-entitled, body/boundary coding scene-bound, self-control burdens recognized, after-scene dignity preserved, internal framing accountable to outer form, visible form non-totalized, boundary and aggression distinguishable, and publicness handled as overlay.

Drift potential increases where re-framing replaces integration, frames are monopolized, asymmetry is moralized instead of regulated, persistence despite self-undercutting appears, temporal costs are externalized, category availability replaces frame breadth, access simulation replaces concrete correction, body/boundary coding becomes person truth, sexed leniency replaces operator reading, one role-position carries disproportionate self-control without dignity recognition, practice labels block reading, visible form is either denied or totalized, boundary and aggression collapse into each other, after-scene dignity fails, or publicness is misread—often along the chaining described in Chapter 18.

#### (6) One-line Marker

Functional practice is defined by governability, not normality: Ω nameable, Θ real, Χ operative, Ψ not substituted, after-scene dignity intact, and publicness kept in proportion.

---

## 20. Minimal Psychology as a Structural Self-Check Adapter

*(Structural alarm; non-diagnostic, non-interpretive)*

### 20.1 Purpose and Boundary

“Minimal psychology” is a name for a structural self-check adapter, not a psychological explanatory layer.

This chapter introduces **minimal psychology** as a **structural self-check adapter** for a specific gap in the model: cases where **drift markers (Chapter 18)** and **viability criteria (Chapter 19)** are already visible, yet the configuration continues unchanged because the description alone no longer interrupts repetition.

Minimal psychology here is **not explanatory**. It is a **late configuration-internal alarm** before critique (Chapter 21) or system-level evaluation (Chapter 22) becomes relevant.

Boundaries remain strict:

* no diagnosis,
* no motive theory,
* no person typing,
* no identity ranking,
* no moral evaluation,
* no therapeutic method,
* no conversion into clinical taxonomy,
* no maturity ranking,
* no adultness verdict,
* no person-level assignment of drift markers.

All outputs remain **scene-bound, reversible, and dignity-preserving**.

This probe does not override scene readability. It is admissible only where structural drift is already legible in enacted form and where further self-description would otherwise risk replacing rather than clarifying that legibility.

The same restriction applies to the sexual drift profiles introduced in Chapters 18 and 19. If asymmetry-switch drift, parity-to-exit, responsibility-to-authority, visible-form fixation, sexed leniency drift, asymmetric self-control burden, boundary-aggression collapse, category monopolization, access entitlement drift, body/boundary person-truth drift, or after-scene dignity failure is present, minimal psychology still does not explain the pattern psychologically. It asks only whether self-description, desire-language, category-language, access-language, body/boundary language, non-binding language, protection-language, or dignity-language is helping the configuration continue despite already visible cost topology.

### 20.2 When This Adapter Activates (Explicit Link to 18/19)

Minimal psychology is **not always relevant**. It activates only when the following condition holds:

> Drift markers from **Chapter 18** are present  
> **and** minimal viability conditions from **Chapter 19** are no longer restoring correction  
> **but** the configuration continues to be carried repeatedly.

Typical activation context:

* Ψ leak has been named, but repetition continues,
* Ω costs are legible, but still accepted, switched, denied, or externalized,
* Θ damage is foreseeable, but stop-capability keeps failing,
* Χ exists formally, but is not enacted in time,
* practice labels continue to block outer-form analysis,
* visible form is either denied or totalized,
* category availability replaces frame breadth or concrete correction,
* access language begins to function as entitlement, deprivation narrative, or simulated counterdesire,
* body/boundary coding begins to function as person truth rather than scene-bound form,
* after-scene dignity fails while internal naming continues to protect the scene,
* sex-coded leniency or blame replaces scene-bound responsibility reading,
* one role-position carries disproportionate self-control burden without dignity recognition,
* boundary-setting, stopping, withdrawal, refusal, resistance, or distance creation can no longer be structurally distinguished from aggressive, punitive, retaliatory, discharge-driven, or escalatory conduct,
* publicness is blamed or ignored while the enacted configuration remains unchanged,
* internal self-description becomes more elaborate while the operator chain continues to narrow,
* asymmetry activation is named but remains unmarked, unbounded, or unrebound,
* parity language is repeatedly used to exit responsibility under unequal cost topology,
* responsibility language is repeatedly converted into control, protection entitlement, or frame authority.

At this point, structural description remains correct—but **no longer sufficient** to interrupt the path.

### 20.3 Guiding Question (Restricted Use)

> **“What structural role is this desire, category, label, or self-description playing in this configuration?”**

The colloquial form “Why do I really desire X?” is admissible only if immediately translated into this structural question. The question is permitted **only** as a *structural probe* under drift persistence.

Constraints:

* it is **hypothetical**, not confessional,
* it targets **pattern continuity**, not inner truth,
* it is asked to test whether desire-language, desire-orientation, category-language, access-language, body/boundary language, non-binding language, protection-language, or dignity-language is functioning as a drift carrier in the configuration,
* it returns attention to enacted form, cost layout, stop-capability, boundary readability, asymmetry handling, after-scene dignity, and accumulated consequence,
* it may not be used to override outer legibility with a deeper self-story,
* it may not be used to explain away asymmetry-switch drift, parity-to-exit, responsibility-to-authority, sexed leniency drift, asymmetric self-control burden, boundary-aggression collapse, category monopolization, access entitlement drift, body/boundary person-truth drift, or after-scene dignity failure as personality, trauma, desire, sex, orientation, authenticity, or identity.

The question is invalid if it produces identity stories, trauma narratives, confession loops, diagnosis claims, justification loops, sex truths, maturity verdicts, adultness rankings, or violence rationalizations. Its only legitimate function is to **re-route attention back to structure**.

### 20.4 Permitted Warning Hypothesis (Narrow, Non-Judging)

Under sustained drift, one limited hypothesis becomes admissible:

> In this configuration, desire-language, category-language, access-language, body/boundary language, or self-description may be functioning as a **drift-maintaining mechanism**  
> rather than as play, exploration, negotiated intensity, bounded practice, marked asymmetry activation, scene-bound body/boundary coding, or D-compatible guided dominance.

This hypothesis does **not** explain desire, category fixation, access pressure, body/boundary coding, humiliation-nearness, or self-control burden. It flags the possibility that one of these languages is now aligned with drift maintenance.

The hypothesis is never confirmed psychologically. It is only **structurally tested** against enacted patterns: repetition, cost concentration, outer legibility denial, visible-form fixation, category monopolization, access entitlement drift, body/boundary person-truth drift, loss of distance, boundary-aggression collapse, after-scene dignity failure, asymmetry escalation, temporal overload, switch drift, parity-to-exit, and responsibility-to-authority.

This is not a person verdict. It is a configuration-level alarm only.

### 20.5 Test Criteria

*(Directly derived from Chapters 18 and 19)*

Minimal psychology engages **only** through observable enactment patterns already described elsewhere. It does not discover hidden causes. It tests whether a language-form is helping a configuration continue despite already visible drift.

#### (1) Repeated D undercutting and after-scene dignity failure

Across scenes:

* enactments repeatedly undermine dignity-in-practice,
* degradation-near, humiliation-near, exposure-near, body-marked, or boundary-marked forms recur without sufficient frame breadth, Χ, Σ, Ψ, or after-scene dignity,
* outer-form naming is blocked by internal labels,
* visible form is either denied or totalized,
* asymmetry is intensified while being denied,
* protection-language, vulnerability-language, guided-dominance language, or play-language is used while non-degradation constraints fail,
* after-costs are carried through shame residue, self-worth leakage, blame reversal, immunity, or person-shrinking.

This maps directly to **Chapter 18 drift chains** where Ψ leak, Ω escalation, humiliation-near overload, and boundary confusion persist, and to **Chapter 19 failure** of D and after-scene dignity as viability constraints.

This does not mean a person has lower dignity. It means the configuration repeatedly fails to preserve Dignity-in-Practice as an enactment constraint.

#### (2) Θ damage despite knowledge

Across time:

* foreseeable harm is explicitly acknowledged,
* repetition continues unchanged,
* accumulation accelerates while stop-capability weakens,
* exit fictions remain active,
* publicness, documentation, bodily effects, category fixation, reputational exposure, or binding residues are minimized until they harden,
* asymmetry activation is repeatedly treated as temporary while its cost effects accumulate.

This is the **Θ overload phase** described in Chapter 18, combined with the **Θ realism failure** marker from Chapter 19.

Reinterpretation may alter meaning, but it does not rewind accumulated effects.

#### (3) Progressive frame narrowing and category monopolization

Across configurations:

* alternatives lose attractiveness or feasibility,
* avoidance and substitution become structurally unavailable,
* one script or category dominates despite rising costs,
* category availability replaces frame breadth or concrete correction,
* practice labels become shields against re-reading,
* internal meaning expands while frame breadth contracts,
* asymmetry activation, parity rhetoric, responsibility language, category-language, access-language, or body/boundary language becomes the default route instead of explicit coordination.

This is **Α fixation** and **category monopolization** combined with loss of functional alternatives.

#### (4) Desire, category, or self-description used against Χ

Across scenes:

* desire is invoked to bypass stopping, hesitation, or meta-commentary,
* distance is treated as betrayal of authenticity,
* “I want this,” “this is who I am,” “this is what this category means,” or “this is what the other really wants” replaces frame analysis,
* internal desire-language prevents outer-form reading,
* category-language blocks cost topology,
* access-language blocks concrete correction,
* body/boundary language blocks scene-bound reconstruction,
* desire-language makes asymmetry activation feel self-justifying rather than markable and re-bindable.

This is **Χ erosion** through self-description. The issue is not desire, category, access, or body/boundary coding itself; the issue is their functioning as anti-distance devices.

#### (5) Publicness displacement

Across scenes or aftermath:

* public reaction is treated as the whole problem,
* or publicness is denied despite documentation, circulation, reputational exposure, or sedimentation,
* the enacted configuration remains unread because the focus moves entirely to audience response,
* publicness is used to avoid naming bodily, reputational, exposure-related, category-bound, access-related, body/boundary-related, or responsibility-related costs already present in the scene.

This is **publicness confusion**: publicity is neither the sole origin nor irrelevant. It is an overlay that can amplify and harden what the scene already presents.

#### (6) Switch drift carried by self-description

Across scenes:

* asymmetry activation is repeatedly described as exception, need, protection, vulnerability, or overload, but not marked, bounded, and re-bound,
* parity language is repeatedly used to deny additional responsibility under unequal cost topology,
* responsibility language is repeatedly used to justify control, protection entitlement, or frame authority,
* the configuration explains these moves through identity, desire, authenticity, care, necessity, fragility, injury, or protection rather than through cost topology.

This criterion activates the self-check only as an alarm. It does not decide what anyone “really wants.” It asks whether self-description is now helping a drift route remain stable.

#### (7) Boundary-aggression collapse carried by self-description

Across scenes:

* stopping, refusal, withdrawal, resistance, boundary-setting, or distance creation is described as aggression without reconstructing the full configuration,
* or aggressive, retaliatory, punitive, discharge-driven, or escalatory conduct is described as mere boundary-setting,
* one role-position’s self-description settles what only frame, cost topology, temporal accumulation, interruption capacity, and after-scene dignity can reconstruct,
* the configuration cannot re-read boundary and aggression without converting the question into blame, danger-labeling, or self-justification.

This criterion does not adjudicate the case. It does not authorize response, coercion, or moral verdict. It only asks whether self-description is now helping the boundary/aggression collapse persist.

### 20.6 Output Format (Invariant, Minimal)

Minimal psychology **never outputs explanation**. It outputs a **structural alarm**, in fixed language:

* “In this configuration, drift persistence is present.”
* “Structural self-correction is failing within the configuration.”
* “Distance (Χ), frame clarity (□), and Θ realism require reactivation.”
* “Internal framing is no longer sufficient to settle the enacted structure.”
* “Outer legibility and cost distribution require re-reading without person-ranking.”
* “Visible form remains readable without being totalized.”
* “Category pressure, access thresholds, and body/boundary coding require re-reading as scene features, not person truths.”
* “After-scene dignity requires re-reading under Θ.”
* “Boundary-setting and aggression require structural distinction; this alarm does not decide the case or authorize response.”
* “Asymmetry activation, if present, requires marking, bounding, and re-binding into Σ/Ψ.”
* “Parity language and responsibility language require re-reading against the sexual cost topology.”

No conclusions about character, pathology, motive, identity, orientation, sex, maturity, adultness, or worth are permitted.

### 20.7 Chapter Closure — Minimal Psychology as Structural Alarm

#### (1) Structural Result

This chapter establishes minimal psychology as a **boundary mechanism inside PMS-SEX**, not as an explanatory layer. It becomes relevant only when drift dynamics (Chapter 18) and viability criteria (Chapter 19) are already structurally legible, yet repetition continues unchanged. The result is a precise repositioning: minimal psychology does not explain why drift occurs, but marks the point where **structural description alone no longer interrupts reenactment**. Its role is to signal internal correction failure before critique turns outward.

The chapter also clarifies that this alarm does not override scene readability. It does not replace enacted form with inner truth; it only tests whether self-description, desire-language, category-language, access-language, body/boundary language, protection-language, non-binding language, or dignity-language is now helping the configuration continue.

The drift vocabulary sharpens this alarm: where asymmetry becomes leverage, parity becomes exit, responsibility becomes authority, category availability replaces frame breadth, access becomes entitlement, body/boundary coding becomes person truth, self-control burden becomes unrecognized, boundary and aggression become unreadable, or after-scene dignity fails, the self-check does not ask for a deeper motive. It asks whether the configuration has lost the capacity to re-read its own cost topology.

#### (2) Cost Distribution

Even without psychological explanation, costs accumulate concretely:

* through **Θ (temporality):** foreseeable harm continues to accrue despite explicit awareness,
* through **Χ erosion:** stop-capability weakens as repetition normalizes urgency, authenticity, inevitability, or self-description,
* through **□ narrowing:** alternative frames lose accessibility as one script dominates,
* through **Α fixation:** repetition makes the narrow route easier to repeat,
* through **category monopolization:** category availability replaces frame breadth or concrete correction,
* through **Ω concentration:** access, exposure, definition, and repair burdens distribute unevenly,
* through **access entitlement drift:** access thresholds are redescribed as deprivation, injury, or simulated counterdesire,
* through **body/boundary person-truth drift:** body-state, exposure, shame, recognition, or boundary-form becomes person truth,
* through **outer-form denial:** internal labels prevent reading of enacted form,
* through **visible-form fixation:** the most visible action-form is treated as the whole configuration,
* through **publicness confusion:** publicity is treated as either the whole cause or irrelevant,
* through **D-in-Practice failure:** the configuration repeatedly fails to preserve non-degradation under asymmetry via boundary violations, humiliation-near dynamics, degradation-near scripts, or after-scene dignity failure,
* through **boundary-aggression collapse:** stopping, refusal, withdrawal, resistance, boundary-setting, and aggressive, punitive, retaliatory, discharge-driven, or escalatory conduct become structurally confused,
* through **asymmetry-switch drift:** asymmetry activation becomes repeatable without re-binding,
* through **parity-to-exit:** equality or mutuality language denies additional responsibility under unequal cost topology,
* through **responsibility-to-authority:** required self-binding becomes control or frame authority.

Minimal psychology names these costs without redescribing them as inner deficits.

#### (3) Structural Viability Corridor

**Viability increases where** the alarm restores distance, reopens frame breadth, re-centers Θ realism, permits outer-form reading, keeps visible form serious but non-totalizing, keeps publicness in proportion, makes sexual cost topology explicit, returns category pressure, access thresholds, and body/boundary coding to scene-bound readability, restores after-scene dignity, distinguishes boundary-setting from aggression, and interrupts repetition without converting the situation into identity narrative.

**Drift begins where** the alarm is ignored, domesticated, moralized, or turned into self-interpretation, allowing Α fixation, Θ accumulation, Ω concentration, category monopolization, access entitlement drift, body/boundary person-truth drift, outer-form denial, visible-form fixation, boundary-aggression collapse, switch drift, parity-to-exit, responsibility-to-authority, and dignity erosion to continue under the appearance of insight.

The corridor remains praxeological: it distinguishes interruption from continuation, not health from pathology.

#### (4) Entry Guard

* **Χ (Distance):** preserved by using the “why” question strictly as a meta-interrupt to reenactment, not as a fusion with desire, category, identity, sex, or deeper truth. Χ also requires that boundary-setting, stopping, refusal, withdrawal, resistance, and distance creation remain distinguishable from aggressive, punitive, retaliatory, discharge-driven, or escalatory conduct.
* **Reversibility:** preserved by keeping all hypotheses hypothetical and configuration-bound, while explicitly acknowledging that accumulated effects do not reset through reinterpretation.
* **D (Dignity-in-Practice):** preserved by refusing explanation, typing, diagnosis, sex truth, identity ranking, maturity ranking, adultness verdict, or evaluation of persons, and by limiting the alarm to protection against further structural self-undercutting.

#### (5) One-line Marker

Minimal psychology in PMS-SEX activates when drift persists despite clarity: it does not explain desire, but signals that the configuration is no longer structurally self-correcting.

---

## 21. Dignity-in-Practice (D) in the Explicit Sexual Frame

*(Protection and critique module, non-moralizing)*

**NOTE:** In *Maturity in Practice (MIP)*, “dignity” is split into **ontological dignity** (non-negotiable human worth) and **praxeological dignity** (*Dignity-in-Practice, D*). PMS-SEX uses **D only in the praxeological sense**: a constraint on *how* sexual practice is enacted. **D never justifies humiliation, degradation, shaming, diagnosis, identity ranking, maturity ranking, or person-level valuation** as a mode of coordination or critique.

### 21.1 Purpose of the Module

This chapter defines **Dignity-in-Practice (D)** as a structural minimum condition for explicit sexual practice under asymmetry. It functions both as protection against unwarranted degradation and as a formal basis for legitimate critique, without moral psychology and without person-level valuation.

The module is scene-bound: it evaluates enactments inside frames, not people as global entities.

Dignity-in-Practice does not require denying outer form. A scene may remain externally legible as a humiliation-form, degradation-form, asymmetry-form, possession-form, control-form, exposure-form, authority-form, body-form, boundary-form, or permission-image without this implying a judgment about anyone’s worth, motives, identity, orientation, maturity, adultness, or dignity. The question is not what persons are, but how a configuration handles asymmetry in enactment.

The relevant structural criterion is sharper: Dignity-in-Practice blocks not only degradation and humiliation, but also the sexual drift triad in which **asymmetry becomes leverage, parity becomes exit, or responsibility becomes authority**. Given the preceding drift logic, it also blocks after-scene dignity failure, sexed leniency drift, asymmetric self-control burden, boundary-aggression collapse, outer-form denial, and visible-form totalization.

### 21.2 Principle: D Applies in Enactment, Not as Status

(Dignity-in-Practice: contextual meaning = enacted restraint and non-degradation under asymmetry.)

In this configuration, two constraints must be kept distinct:

* **No entitlement to the person**
  No authority over motives, worth, identity, biography, orientation, body, desire, preference, category, boundary, or “what someone really is.”

* **Claim to D in enactment**
  Restraint, respect, non-degradation, stop-capability, boundary readability, and dignity-preserving handling of asymmetry within the accepted frame.

D is therefore not a virtue, not a character trait, not adultness, and not a moral rank. It is a practice condition testable only in enactment and temporal carryover: whether the configuration preserves non-degradation while carrying real asymmetries.

This distinction also protects outer-form analysis. Naming an externally readable humiliation-form, degradation-form, asymmetry-form, possession-form, control-form, authority-form, exposure-form, body-form, boundary-form, or permission-image is not itself a violation of the model’s anti-moral stance. The violation would lie in converting scene analysis into person-ranking, humiliation, diagnosis, maturity ranking, adultness verdict, identity verdict, or moral contempt.

D also does not require symmetrical burdens. It requires that unequal burdens not be externalized as humiliation, abandonment, leverage, control, authority, sex-coded leniency, unrecognized self-control burden, or after-scene dignity failure.

### 21.3 Minimal Formula of D (PMS-Compliant)

(Asymmetry: contextual meaning = gradients of access, exposure, obligation, and cost-bearing.)  
(Distance: contextual meaning = stop-capability and meta-position within ongoing praxis.)  
(Self-Binding: contextual meaning = identity-relevant commitment over time.)  
(Temporality: contextual meaning = accumulation, irreversibility, and trajectory.)  
(Frame: contextual meaning = the rule-and-role grammar that makes enactment legible.)

D-compliance becomes structurally legible where the configuration carries the following constraints:

* **Ω is explicit:** asymmetry is recognized and governed, not denied, romanticized, hidden under pseudo-symmetry, or activated as unmarked leverage.
* **Χ is operative:** stop-capability, meta-position, interruption, boundary-setting, refusal, withdrawal, and distance creation remain usable in practice, not only as claims.
* **No covert Ψ demand:** meaning, possession, self-worth, and identity claims are not smuggled into the frame.
* **Θ is carried:** repetition, consequences, downstream costs, exit realism, and after-scene dignity remain nameable.
* **Outer form remains readable as a PMS-SEX guard:** internal framing, practice labels, or later recontextualization do not erase enacted form.
* **Visible form remains non-totalizing:** visible action-form is taken seriously without being treated as the whole configuration.
* **Asymmetry activation is marked and bounded:** real Ω/Θ overload may require activation, but it must be explicit, limited, and re-bound.
* **Category, access, and body/boundary pressures remain scene-bound:** category availability does not monopolize the broader sexual field, access remains threshold-language rather than entitlement, and body/boundary coding does not become person truth.
* **Humiliation-nearness remains D-compatible only under after-scene dignity:** guided dominance, negotiated boundary-nearness, exposure, shame transformation, or humiliation-near play must remain bounded, re-readable, and carryable after Θ without person-shrinking or self-worth leakage.
* **Sexed leniency drift is blocked:** leniency, exception, contextualization, blame, and relief track scene, cost, capacity, and responsibility rather than sex-coded automatic protection or blame overload.
* **Asymmetric self-control burden is recognized:** higher Χ/Ψ burden requires higher dignity recognition, not lower recognition.
* **Boundary and aggression remain distinguishable:** stopping, refusal, withdrawal, resistance, boundary-setting, and distance creation are not collapsed into aggression; aggression, punishment, retaliation, discharge, or escalation are not immunized as mere boundary-setting.
* **Parity does not become exit:** equality language must not deny additional responsibility under unequal sexual cost topology.
* **Responsibility does not become authority:** required self-binding must not become control, frame ownership, protection entitlement, or paternalistic governance.

**Short PMS-SEX application formula:**

> **D-in-Practice in PMS-SEX = explicit Ω + operative Χ + no covert Ψ demand under Θ + after-scene dignity + marked/bounded asymmetry activation + no parity-to-exit + no responsibility-to-authority + boundary/aggression distinction + outer-form readability without visible-form totalization.**

This is not an ethical ideal. It is a viability constraint: without these conditions, the configuration easily drifts into coercion, humiliation, degradation, cost externalization, abandonment, category monopolization, access entitlement, body/boundary person-truth, asymmetry leverage, parity-exit, or authority-conversion while still narrating itself as “consensual,” “just play,” “devotion,” “service,” “authenticity,” “casual,” “mutual,” “guided,” or “D-compatible.”

The same restriction applies to disturbance or path-cost language. Higher stabilization burden may describe a configuration’s structural demands, but it does not lower dignity, reduce personhood, rank identity, authorize humiliation, or justify violence.

### 21.4 Reference Case: Client Configuration (Not Exclusive)

This subsection is a clarification case, not a special right and not an exclusivity claim. It is used because the frame often makes Ω explicit and Ψ suspension declarative, which makes D violations and D compliance structurally testable.

#### (1) Structural baseline

(Frame: contextual meaning = the rule-and-role grammar that defines what counts as an event.)  
(Asymmetry: contextual meaning = gradients of access, exposure, obligation, and cost-bearing.)

In this configuration:

* Ω is highly explicit: payment, choice, access, exposure, exit margins,
* □ is formalized: roles and boundaries are legible,
* Ψ is intended to be suspended: the frame is not designed as identity-binding,
* publicness may appear as an overlay: stigma, documentation, reputation, or institutional visibility,
* outer legibility remains possible: the scene may still present visible asymmetry, exposure, role-form, body-form, boundary-form, or permission-image,
* sexual cost topology remains active: bodily, reputational, exposure-related, publicness-related, after-scene, and exit-related costs do not disappear because the frame is explicit,
* after-scene dignity remains relevant: suspension of Ψ does not make temporal carryover irrelevant.

Precisely for that reason, D is not “automatic,” but it is unusually observable: the gap between declared frame, enacted mode, cost topology, and after-scene carryover is easy to see.

#### (2) Protection against unwarranted degradation

In this configuration, critique or devaluation is not justified when:

* the frame is respected: rules and boundaries are kept,
* there is no boundary violation and no pressure beyond the agreed asymmetry,
* there is no covert meaning demand: no Ψ leak,
* there is no manipulation via withdrawal or post-hoc humiliation,
* outer-form naming is not converted into person-shaming,
* visible form is not totalized into a person verdict,
* after-scene dignity remains intact,
* asymmetry is marked and governed rather than used as leverage,
* responsibility remains self-binding and does not become authority over the other role-position,
* self-control burdens are not hidden, displaced, or converted into lower dignity recognition,
* leniency or critique tracks scene, cost, capacity, and responsibility rather than stigma, sex-coded expectation, or role contempt.

Stigma, mockery, or moral devaluation function here as a systemic frame overlay rather than as legitimate critique. They do not describe the configuration; they attempt to punish it from outside the frame.

At the same time, protection against stigma does not require denying structure. A configuration can be externally readable as an asymmetry-form, exposure-form, body-form, boundary-form, or permission-image without that readability authorizing contempt, shaming, or person-level judgment.

### 21.5 When Critique Is Not Justified

Critique is structurally invalid when all of the following are true in this configuration:

* **Frame respect:** rules, boundaries, timing, and exit conditions are kept.
* **No D withdrawal in enactment:** no humiliation, degradation, or shaming is used as a steering instrument.
* **No after-scene dignity failure:** the scene remains carryable after Θ without person-shrinking, shame residue, blame reversal, immunity, or self-worth leakage.
* **No Ω escalation:** no pushing beyond the agreed asymmetry, no pressure against stop markers.
* **No Ψ leak:** no intimacy, possession, self-worth, or identity demand across the frame boundary.
* **Outer-form naming remains non-punitive:** structural readability is not used to shame or rank persons.
* **Visible form remains non-totalizing:** the visible action-form is read without being treated as the whole configuration or person truth.
* **Publicness is not weaponized:** visibility, reputation, or stigma is not used as leverage or punishment.
* **No unmarked asymmetry activation:** any activation under Ω/Θ pressure is marked, bounded, and re-bound.
* **No category/access/body-boundary drift:** category availability remains proportional, access remains threshold-language rather than entitlement, and body/boundary coding remains scene-bound rather than person truth.
* **No sexed leniency drift:** leniency, blame, exception, or contextualization tracks scene, cost, capacity, and responsibility rather than sex-coded readability.
* **No asymmetric self-control invisibilization:** any disproportionate Χ/Ψ burden remains nameable and dignity-recognized.
* **No boundary-aggression collapse:** stopping, refusal, withdrawal, resistance, boundary-setting, and distance creation remain structurally distinguishable from aggression, punishment, retaliation, discharge, or escalation.
* **No parity-to-exit:** equality or mutuality language is not used to deny responsibility under unequal cost topology.
* **No responsibility-to-authority:** responsibility is carried as self-binding rather than control.

In these cases, critique is frame-external or moralizing rather than praxeological. It does not target drift or harm mechanisms; it targets person-status.

### 21.6 When Critique Becomes Structurally Legible

Critique becomes structurally legible when at least one of the following markers is present, because each marker signals drift into harm-relevant dynamics. These markers do not diagnose persons and do not authorize retaliation, humiliation, coercion, or practical instruction. They make D-relevant scene structure readable.

#### (1) Covert self-binding demand (Ψ leak)

(Self-Binding: contextual meaning = identity-relevant commitment over time.)

In this configuration:

* meaning, possession, or identity claims exceed the agreed frame,
* emotional attachment becomes an implicit counter-performance,
* “this must mean more” is demanded while suspension is asserted,
* local enactments are treated as identity proofs.

This is not “having feelings.” It is a structural mismatch: binding is introduced inside a frame that cannot carry binding cleanly.

#### (2) Power / choice abuse (Ω escalation)

(Asymmetry: contextual meaning = gradients of access, exposure, obligation, and cost-bearing.)

In this configuration:

* situational advantages are used against explicit or implicit stop markers,
* boundary tests and pressure normalize “just this once” drift,
* definitional control shifts without rule update,
* exposure, access, or repair burdens are unevenly distributed while the frame narrates neutrality.

Here, Ω becomes a steering variable instead of a governed layout.

#### (3) Pseudo-symmetry

(Frame: contextual meaning = the grammar that defines what counts as inside/outside.)

In this configuration:

* equality rhetoric substitutes for explicit asymmetry governance,
* cost, exposure, and risk gradients are made unnameable inside the frame,
* consent or mutuality language is used to block analysis of unequal after-costs,
* non-binding language is used to deny continuing Θ consequences.

Pseudo-symmetry increases conflict load because the configuration must not name what is structurally doing the steering.

#### (4) Irresponsibility under Θ

(Temporality: contextual meaning = accumulation, irreversibility, and trajectory.)

In this configuration:

* foreseeable consequences are ignored or denied,
* costs are externalized: bodily, social, reputational, exposure-related, publicness-related, category-bound, access-related, body/boundary-related, or binding-related,
* repetition persists despite clear harm trajectories,
* exit is narrated as reset while accumulation continues,
* after-scene dignity is treated as optional rather than as Θ realism.

Here, critique is not morality but structural protection: it targets cost relocation, exit fiction, and after-scene dignity failure.

#### (5) Outer-form denial

(Frame / Recontextualization / Distance: contextual meaning = enacted form, later redescription, and re-reading capacity.)

In this configuration:

* internal labels such as play, kink, devotion, service, discipline, authenticity, consent, guided dominance, humiliation-nearness, or casualness are used to end structural reading,
* outer legibility is treated as hostile, irrelevant, or merely public misunderstanding,
* recontextualization changes the story while the enacted action-form and cost layout remain effective.

Here, critique protects the model’s scene-readability: internal framing may be real, but it does not erase outer structural form.

#### (6) Visible-form fixation

(Frame / Asymmetry / Temporality / Distance: contextual meaning = visible action-form within broader scene structure.)

In this configuration:

* the most visible action-form is treated as the whole structure,
* frame history, non-event pressure, internal framing, category formation, asymmetry distribution, self-control burden, and temporal accumulation are under-read,
* visible outer form becomes person verdict rather than scene evidence,
* correction targets only the visible layer while cost topology remains unread.

Here, critique protects D by preventing outer readability from becoming person reduction.

#### (7) Publicness weaponization or publicness denial

(Frame overlay: contextual meaning = visibility, circulation, documentation, reputation, and sedimentation.)

In this configuration:

* publicity is used to shame, threaten, expose, or punish,
* or publicity is dismissed as irrelevant despite amplification, documentation, and reputational sedimentation,
* public reaction replaces analysis of the enacted configuration.

Here, critique targets the misuse or denial of publicness as overlay. Publicity may intensify consequence; it need not create the primary form.

#### (8) Category, access, or body/boundary drift

(Difference / Attractor / Asymmetry: contextual meaning = category formation, access threshold, and scene-bound body/boundary coding.)

In this configuration:

* category availability replaces frame breadth or concrete correction,
* access language becomes entitlement, deprivation narrative, or simulated counterdesire,
* body-state, exposure, shame, recognition, or boundary-form becomes person truth,
* a permission-image is treated as if it settled consent, encounter, or the other’s desire.

Here, critique targets category, access, and body/boundary pressures becoming dignity-relevant drift rather than scene-bound features.

#### (9) Positive dominance / humiliation-nearness losing D

(Dignity-in-Practice / Distance / Self-Binding: contextual meaning = non-degradation under guided intensity or humiliation-near form.)

In this configuration:

* guided dominance, negotiated boundary-nearness, exposure, or humiliation-near play is treated as immune because it is internally named as play,
* stop-capability, meta-position, or after-scene dignity weakens,
* humiliation-nearness leaks into self-worth, identity proof, shame residue, or person-shrinking,
* the scene remains intelligible only by denying outer form or denying after-costs.

Here, critique does not deny that humiliation-nearness may be D-compatible. It targets the point where D can no longer be preserved under Θ.

#### (10) Sexed leniency drift

(Asymmetry / Responsibility / Self-Binding: contextual meaning = responsibility distribution under sex-coded readability.)

In this configuration:

* leniency or blame tracks sex-coded readability rather than scene, cost, capacity, or responsibility,
* escalation by one role-position is contextualized while another role-position’s boundary, refusal, or distance is over-blamed,
* vulnerability language, danger language, protection language, or emotionality language replaces operator reading,
* responsibility is displaced through automatic relief or automatic suspicion.

Here, critique protects D by requiring that relief, blame, exception, and responsibility remain configuration-bound rather than sex-coded.

#### (11) Asymmetric self-control burden

(Distance / Self-Binding / Dignity-in-Practice: contextual meaning = unequal restraint, de-escalation, and self-binding load.)

In this configuration:

* one role-position must carry disproportionate restraint, de-escalation, non-reaction, interruption discipline, or distance,
* another role-position’s escalation is more easily framed as injury, overwhelm, exception, authenticity, or context,
* self-control expectation erases the cost of carrying self-control,
* higher Χ/Ψ burden is paired with lower dignity recognition.

Here, critique targets a D failure: greater self-control burden requires greater dignity recognition, not less.

#### (12) Boundary-aggression collapse

(Distance / Asymmetry / Dignity-in-Practice: contextual meaning = stop-capability, cost topology, and boundary readability.)

In this configuration:

* stopping, refusal, withdrawal, resistance, boundary-setting, or distance creation is too quickly read as aggression,
* or aggression, punishment, retaliation, discharge, or escalation is framed as mere boundary-setting,
* the scene can no longer distinguish interruption from attack, or attack from interruption,
* labels settle what only frame, cost topology, temporal accumulation, interruption capacity, and after-scene dignity can reconstruct.

Here, critique does not adjudicate the concrete case or authorize response. It targets a failure of D-relevant scene readability.

#### (13) Asymmetry-switch drift

(Asymmetry / Temporality / Integration / Self-Binding: contextual meaning = asymmetry activation under consequence pressure and its re-binding conditions.)

In this configuration:

* real or invoked body-, exposure-, reputational-, category-bound, access-related, body/boundary-related, or Θ-consequence asymmetry is activated as exception,
* the activation is not marked as exceptional or structurally necessary,
* the activation remains repeatable,
* parity language remains available for access, autonomy, or mutuality,
* responsibility is shifted rather than re-bound into Σ/Ψ.

Here, critique targets the substitution of coordination by unmarked asymmetry activation. The drift is not asymmetry activation as such; the drift is activation without marking, bounding, and re-binding.

#### (14) Parity-to-exit drift

(Frame / Asymmetry / Temporality / Self-Binding: contextual meaning = equality rhetoric under unequal sexual cost topology.)

In this configuration:

* parity, mutuality, autonomy, or consent language is used to deny additional responsibility,
* unequal bodily, reputational, publicness-related, category-bound, access-related, body/boundary-related, or temporal costs are flattened by formal equality claims,
* the role-position with greater externalization capacity exits responsibility by invoking symmetry.

Here, critique targets equality-language functioning as responsibility displacement. Parity binds reciprocity only when it coordinates cost topology; it becomes drift when it exits it.

#### (15) Responsibility-to-authority drift

(Self-Binding / Distance / Asymmetry / Frame: contextual meaning = responsibility under asymmetry mistranslated as control.)

In this configuration:

* required responsibility under sexual asymmetry is acknowledged,
* but responsibility is converted into control, frame authority, protection entitlement, or paternalistic governance,
* care becomes control,
* protection becomes ownership,
* restraint becomes entitlement to define the other role-position.

Here, critique targets the conversion of Ψ/Χ responsibility into authority. Responsibility under asymmetry requires stronger self-binding, not greater command.

### 21.7 Asymmetries on Both Sides (Anti-Reduction)

Asymmetry does not imply one-sidedness. In many explicit frames, both sides face asymmetries, but in different channels:

* different costs,
* different risks,
* different exposures,
* different exit margins and recovery conditions,
* different capacities to define, refuse, publicize, repair, or absorb consequences,
* different category pressures,
* different access thresholds,
* different body/boundary overhangs,
* different after-scene costs,
* different self-control burdens,
* different capacities to activate asymmetry,
* different capacities to externalize costs through parity rhetoric,
* different capacities to convert responsibility into authority.

Adulthood in PMS-SEX is not maintained by symmetry fictions. It is maintained by explicit asymmetry management within the frame. A symmetry claim does not replace responsibility; it often obscures it.

Outer legibility also does not imply one-sided blame. A scene can show visible asymmetry without that visibility settling culpability, worth, motive, identity, maturity, or adultness. It only tells the analysis where cost, exposure, leverage, self-control burden, and after-scene dignity must be reconstructed.

### 21.7a EDEN/PFO Reference: Asymmetry Switch in Sexual Frames

PMS–EDEN names the regime-level asymmetry switch. PMS-SEX reads its sexual instantiation only where sexual cost topology makes the mechanism domain-salient.

In sexual frames, real body-, exposure-, reputational-, publicness-related, category-bound, access-related, body/boundary-related, self-control-related, and consequence-asymmetries may justify marked activation: not all Ω/Θ costs can be carried symmetrically.

The switch is therefore not illegitimate as such. It becomes dignity-relevant where activation is unmarked, repeatable, and responsibility-shifting. In such cases, asymmetry no longer reopens coordination; it replaces coordination. The scene preserves parity language while distributing costs asymmetrically.

Sexual reciprocity also fails through the counter-move. A role-position may invoke parity to deny additional responsibility under unequal sexual cost topology: “it was mutual,” “we are equal,” “the other is autonomous,” “it was casual,” or “no one owes anything.” Or required responsibility may be converted into authority: protection entitlement, control, frame ownership, or paternalistic governance.

Dignity-in-Practice requires these drifts to be blocked. One role-position must not convert asymmetry activation into an unmarked lever. Another must not convert greater externalizability into parity-exit or required responsibility into authority. A role-position assigned greater Χ/Ψ burden must not receive lower dignity recognition. A role-position receiving leniency must not be relieved by sex-coded readability rather than scene-bound responsibility analysis.

Sexual reciprocity under real asymmetry does not require equal burdens. It requires non-externalization of unequal burdens. In EDEN-compatible terms: asymmetry is not the failure; false coordination of real asymmetry is the failure.

This subsection is a reference bridge, not an operator expansion. The switch labels remain paper-internal drift markers and do not add to PMS.

### 21.7b Sexual Cost Topology and Asymmetry-Specific Responsibility

PMS-SEX treats sexual costs as role-distributed and trajectory-sensitive. The relevant question is not whether both role-positions carry identical costs, but whether each position carries the self-binding required by its own cost, power, exit, and externalization profile.

One role-position may carry higher bodily non-delegability: pregnancy possibility, bodily aftereffects, cyclicity, injury risk, exposure, reputational sedimentation, bodily consequence, and social readability. Another role-position may carry higher responsibility where it has greater exit capacity, lower bodily overhang, more plausible denial, more frame-control options, lower visibility, or greater ability to convert responsibility into authority.

After Chapters 15–20, the cost topology must also include category pressure, access-threshold pressure, body/boundary coding, permission-image effects, self-control burden, boundary/aggression readability, and after-scene dignity. These are not new operators and not person measures. They are cost-topological channels: ways in which consequences attach, become readable, or become externalizable under Ω/Θ.

These costs are not equal in content. But sexual reciprocity under real asymmetry does not require equal content. It requires that neither side externalizes its own asymmetry-specific burden. The bodily-consequence-bearing role-position must not use asymmetry activation as unmarked leverage. The externalization-capable role-position must not use parity as exit or responsibility as authority. A role-position carrying greater self-control burden must not be denied recognition for carrying it. A role-position receiving contextualization must not receive automatic relief where its own structuring effects remain active.

The possible consequences differ as well. Unmarked asymmetry activation may weaken trust in legitimate activation, turn protection into leverage, and displace self-binding. Parity-to-exit may make bodily, reputational, category-bound, access-related, or body/boundary costs appear voluntarily assumed and therefore externally abandoned. Responsibility-to-authority may turn care into control and protection into governance. Sexed leniency drift may make responsibility follow role readability rather than operator load. Asymmetric self-control burden may require one role-position to preserve Χ/Ψ while lowering its dignity recognition. Boundary-aggression collapse may make stopping, refusal, withdrawal, or distance unreadable as boundary rather than attack. Each route produces dignity risk by preserving surface order while blocking Σ/Ψ coordination.

The general formula is:

> **Each role-position is accountable to the self-binding required by its own cost, power, exit, and externalization profile.**

### 21.7c Cost Factors by Role-Position

The following table is not a taxonomy of persons. It is a role-position grid for reading sexual cost topology. In concrete scenes, the positions must be mapped by actual cost, capacity, exposure, exit, and externalization structure, not assigned by identity, sex, gender, orientation, or self-description alone.

| Cost / drift axis | Body-consequence-bearing role-position | Externalization-capable role-position |
| - | - | - |
| Bodily Θ | higher non-delegable bodily overhang possible | often lower bodily overhang, but not zero |
| Exposure Ω | higher visible/social/reputational sedimentation possible | exposure may arise through accusation, responsibility, public framing, or authority suspicion |
| Exit | exit may remain bodily/reputationally costly | exit may be cheaper, more deniable, or more narratively available |
| Category pressure | body/boundary categories may become person-truth | access/counterdesire categories may replace concrete correction |
